As noted in the published introduction, this tс╣Ыca shows a high degree of unity. To start with, every p─Бda but 2 (of 12), begins with a form of the 2nd sg. prn.: mostly nom. t u v├бm (28b, d, 29a, c, 30a) but also gen, t├бva (28a, 29b, d), with the final hemistich breaking the pattern with a single acc. t u v─Б╠Бm (distracted; see comm. ad vs. 24 above) in c and a single dat. t├║bhya in d. Only 28c and 30b fail to open with such a form (and 28c has the enclitic te later in the p─Бda). In addition, all 3 vss. contain the voc. pavam─Бna (28c, 29d, 30b), and all three also have forms of v├н┼Ыva- 28b, d, 29a, 30d). Note also that v├н┼Ыvasya bh├║vanasya in the first vs. (28b) is echoed by v├н┼Ыv─Б bh├║van─Бni in the last (30d), and that v├нdharmaс╣Зi (29b) is taken up by better specified r├бjaso v├нdharmaс╣Зi (30a); cf. also t├бvem─Б╠Бh (28a, 29b) varied by t├║bhyem─Б╠Бс╕е (30d).

In terms of contents, the tс╣Ыca insistently asserts SomaтАЩs universal rule over all cosmic elements.

Griffith

Thou in the filter, Soma Pavamana, art purified to support the region for the Gods.
The chief, the longing ones have sought to hold thee fast, and all these living creatures have been turned to thee.

Geldner

Du wirst in der Seihe, in der ganzen Ausbreitung des Raums, f├╝r die G├╢tter gel├дutert, Soma Pavamana. Dich nahmen zuerst die Usij in Besitz; dir sind alle diese Welten untergeordnet.

Grassmann

Gereinigt wirst den G├╢ttern du, o flammender, o Soma, in der Seihe in der L├╝fte Raum, Zuerst ergriffen, Indu, dich die heischenden, und alle diese Wesen streben hin zu dir.

The hymnic visions, bellowing [/in their longing], have roared together. The thoughts lick the child who always excites wonder. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the tight structure of the preceding tс╣Ыca, we have returned to the lax stringing together of soma tropes. There is a lot of noise-making in 31 (b cakradat, c v─Бva┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бan┼лс╣гata), which is slightly echoed in 33 (b k├бnikradat).

Otherwise I see nothing particularly unifying.

As for external connections, GEN niс╣гkс╣Ыt├бm тИЪy─Б in 32d is found also in 7b and 16a, and of course much of the soma lexicon is repeated elsewhere.

Griffith

Onward the Singer travels o’er the fleecy sieve. the Tawny Steer hath bellowed in the wooden vats.
Hymns have been sung aloud in resonant harmony, and holy songs kiss him, the Child who claims our praise.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe invests himself with the rays of the sun stretching out the triple thread in the way he knows; guiding the recent adorations of the truthful (worshipper), the protection of women passes to the consecrated (vessel).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He has enveloped himself with the rays of the sun, stretching his own threefold thread, in the way that is known.
Leading the newer directives of truth, as a husband he proceeds to the rendezvous with his wives.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although the standard interpr. of y├бth─Б vid├й here makes Soma subj. of the verb (e.g., Geldner тАЬwie er es verstehtтАЭ), p─Бda-final y├бth─Б vid├й is a common tag (I.127.4, 132.2, etc.) with a passive reading of the verb: тАЬas is known, in the way that is known.тАЭ The тАЬdirectives of truthтАЭ (с╣Ыt├бsya pra┼Ы├нс╣гaс╕е) are convincingly identified as the hymns by L├╝ders (469-70), as the adj. n├бv─лyas-, a standard descriptor of hymns in the fem., suggests.

I assume that the тАЬthreefold threadтАЭ (t├бntum тАж trivс╣Ыt├бm) refers to the three soma pressings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the tight structure of the preceding tс╣Ыca, we have returned to the lax stringing together of soma tropes. There is a lot of noise-making in 31 (b cakradat, c v─Бva┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бan┼лс╣гata), which is slightly echoed in 33 (b k├бnikradat).

Otherwise I see nothing particularly unifying.

As for external connections, GEN niс╣гkс╣Ыt├бm тИЪy─Б in 32d is found also in 7b and 16a, and of course much of the soma lexicon is repeated elsewhere.

Griffith

He hath assumed the rays of Surya for his robe, spinning, as he knows bow, the triply-twisted thread.
He, guiding to the newest rules of Holy Law, comes as the Women’s Consort to the special place.

Er umkleidet sich mit den Sonnenstrahlen, den dreifachen Faden ausspannend, wie er es versteht. Der Opferordnung Vorschriften aufs neue leitend geht er als Gatte zum Treffort seiner Frauen.

Er hat sich mit der Sonne Strahlen rings umh├╝llt, den dreigetheilten Faden webend, wie gewohnt; Des Opfers neuste Ordnung leitend eilet er als Gatte hin zu seiner Frauen Brautgemach.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sovereign of rivers flows pure, the lord of heaven goes with a shout by the paths of the sacrifice; the thousand-streamed green-tinted (Soma) is poured out, uttering a sound while being filtered, the bringer of wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The king of rivers, the lord of heaven purifies himself. He proceeds along the paths of truth, ever roaring.
The tawny one is poured around with his thousand streams as he is being purified, begetting speech, bringing goods near at hand. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the tight structure of the preceding tс╣Ыca, we have returned to the lax stringing together of soma tropes. There is a lot of noise-making in 31 (b cakradat, c v─Бva┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бan┼лс╣гata), which is slightly echoed in 33 (b k├бnikradat).

Otherwise I see nothing particularly unifying.

As for external connections, GEN niс╣гkс╣Ыt├бm тИЪy─Б in 32d is found also in 7b and 16a, and of course much of the soma lexicon is repeated elsewhere.

Griffith

On flows the King of rivers and the Lord of heaven: he follows with a shout the paths of Holy Law.
The Golden-hued is poured forth, with his hundred streams, Wealth-bringer, lifting up his voice while purified.

Geldner

Er l├дutert sich, der K├╢nig der Gew├дsser, der Herr des Himmels, er geht br├╝llend auf den Pfaden der Opferordnung. In tausend G├╝ssen wird der Goldgelbe ausgegossen; die Rede bringt er hervor, w├дhrend er gel├дutert wird, zu Reichtum kommend.

Grassmann

Der Str├╢me K├╢nig rieselt hell, des Himmels Herr, und schreitet wiehernd auf des Opfers Pfaden hin; In tausend Str├╢men fliesset hin der goldene, Gesang erzeugend, flammend, reich mit Gut versehn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPurified (Soma), you pour forth abundant juice; like the wonderful sun (you approach) the fleecy filters; purified by the hands of the priests, expressed with the stones you flow for a mighty wealth-yielding conflict.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purifying yourself as a great flood, brilliant like the sun, you run across the fleecy filters.
Hand-purified by the men, pressed by the stones, you dash for the great rich prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation does not make sufficiently clear (or clear at all) that p├бvam─Бna is a voc. Better tr. тАЬSelf-purifying one, as a great flood you run тАжтАЭ With Geldner and Renou I take m├бhy ├бrс╣Зaс╕е тАЬgreat floodтАЭ as a nom., coreferential with the 2nd sg. subj. The statement тАЬyou are the seaтАЭ (29a tv├бс╣Г samudr├│ asi) gives semantic support to the coreferential reading, though the two words (samudr├б- and ├бrс╣Зas-) are different. By contrast, L├╝ders (204, 239; sim. Ober II.152 n. 111) takes it as acc. of extent, indicating the space that the soma traverses, with the тАЬfiltersтАЭ of b parallel to it in a simile: тАЬdu durchl├дufst die grosse Flut, wie die strahlende Sonne die wollenen Seihen.тАЭ This interpr. requires that the real filter (the sheepтАЩs fleece) that the real soma ordinarily traverses be part of the simile, expressing what the sun crosses, while the metaphorical filter (тАЬthe great floodтАЭ) is part of the frame, where the real soma is crossing it. This is either very clever poetics, with several levels of metaphor below the surface simile - or an indication that his interpr. is incorrect. IтАЩm afraid that I incline towards the latter view.

The expression in c g├бbhasti-p┼лto nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е is somewhat curious, since it essentially provides two agents, or agent-like elements, for the p┼лt├б- ppl.: the 1st cmpd member g├бbhasti- and the indep. instr. nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е. (Of course, the men are the agents whose hands are the instruments.) Without the тАШhandтАЩ (g├бbhasti-) we would expect *nс╣Ы╠е╠Б-p┼лta-, like nс╣Ы╠Б-dh┼лta- (1x), nс╣Ы╠Б-с╣г┼лta- (1x)(which, oddly enough, both rhyme with our putative form). Renou has a slightly different interpr., but it has the same configuration. His тАЬpress├й par les seigneurs ├а lтАЩaide des pierresтАЭ construes nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е with what follows, the instr. ├бdribhiс╕е and the ppl. sut├бс╕е, with the two instr. filling the agent and instrument slots respectively. Since nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е is stationed exactly in between the two instrument+ppl. expressions, thereтАЩs no way to tell - though it seems to me somewhat more elegant for nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е to double a cmpd. member rather than morphologically doubling another instrument. Note that ├бdri-с╣гuta- is also attested (2x) and that the same ├бdribhiс╕е sut├бс╕е as here is found in this hymn in 23a..

Jamison Brereton Notes

Nothing much in the way of internal unity or external connection, beyond the obvious soma themes.

Griffith

Fain to be cleansed, thou, Pavamana, pourest out, like wondrous Surya, through the fleece, an ample sea.
Purified with the hands, pressed by the men with stones, thou speedest on to mighty booty-bringing war.

Geldner

O Pavamana, als gro├Яe Flut rinnst du farbenpr├дchtig wie die Sonne durch die Filter aus Schafwolle. Von M├дnnern mit den H├дnden gel├дutert, mit Steinen ausgeschlagen rinnst du zu gro├Яem gl├╝ckbringendem Gewinn.

Grassmann

Im Flammenstrom durchrieselst du das grosse Meer, wie Sonnenglanz im hellen Strome durch das Sieb, Gekl├дrt vom Arm der M├дnner und vom Stein gepresst, ergiesst du dich zu grossem, beutereichem Gut.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou rush, Pavam─Бna, to (bring) food and strength; you alight on the pitchers like a falcon on its nest; (you) the exhilarating effused juice giving exhilaration to Indra, resembling the support of heaven, beholding (all things).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Self-purifying one, you rush toward refreshment and nourishment. Like a falcon in the woods, you sit in the tubs.
For Indra is pressed the exhilarative, exhilarating drink of exhilaration, the utmost prop of heaven, wide-gazing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The accumulation of тИЪmad derivatives is striking: m├бdv─Б m├бdyo m├бdaс╕е. The last, m├бda-, is of course extraordinarily common, and the 2nd m├бdya- reasonably well established (13x). But madv├бn- is found only twice.

For Indra poured as cheering juice to make him glad, as nearest and farseeing bearer-up of heaven.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe seven sister mothers approach the new-born, victorious sagacious infant, Soma, abiding amidst the waters, supporter of water, divine the contemplator of men to make him the ruler of the whole world.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The seven sister mothers: i.e., the seven rivers clothe the Soma with their water

Jamison Brereton

The seven sisters, as mothers, (go) to the newborn child of worthy birth, who is attentive to poetic inspiration,
the heavenly Gandharva of the waters, whose gaze is on menтАФto Soma, for the regulation of all creation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Who the seven sisters (bzw. mothers) are is a matter of dispute: S─Бyaс╣Зa.: the streams or rivers, Geldner: thoughts, Renou (flg. L├╝ders 246): celestial streams/rivers. No one seems to cite the seven milk-cows (sapt├б dhen├бvaс╕е) in vs. 25 of this same hymn, or their multiplied number (thrice seven) in 21. But in this hymn тАЬcowsтАЭ seems the mostly likely immediate referent, esp. given the image of maternal care, whatever those cows may otherwise represent (beyond the milk-mixture).

On the expression in the last p─Бda, see similar phrases in vss. 5 and 28.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Nothing much in the way of internal unity or external connection, beyond the obvious soma themes.

Griffith

The Sisters Seven, the Mothers, stand around the Babe, the noble, new-born Infant, skilled in holy song,
Gandharva of the floods, divine, beholding men, Soma, that he may reign as King of all the world.

Geldner

Sieben Schwestern kommen als M├╝tter zu dem neugeborenen Hauskind, dem redekundigen, dem himmlischen Gandharva der Gew├дsser mit dem Herrenauge, zu dem Soma, damit er ├╝ber die ganze Welt herrsche.

Grassmann

Die M├╝tter, sieben Schwestern eilen hin zum Spross, dem neugebornen, herrlichen, begeisterten, Dem m├дnnerschaunden, himmlischen, der Fluten Herrn, dem Soma, dass er herrsche ├╝ber alle Welt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndu, who are the lord, you go (through) threse worlds, harnessing (to the car) your swift-moving steeds; let them dispense the sweet-flavoured shining liquor, may all men be present Soma, at your worship.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Showing mastery, you speed across these worlds here, o drop, having hitched up your golden fine-feathered (mares).
Let them stream honeyed ghee and milk for you. O Soma, let the separate peoples stay under your commandment. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the first time in this hymn (save for briefly in vs. 18), this tс╣Ыca shows some interest in what Soma might do for us, particularly in the 2nd two vss.

Note in 38 first the enclitic naс╕е and then the 1st pl. opt. sy─Бma. The poet both asks for benefits directly and by implication, in the cmpds with 2nd member -v├нd- тАШfindingтАЩ: g├│vid-, vasuv├нd-, h├нraс╣Зyav├нd-, vi┼Ыvav├нd- тАЬcow-finding, goods-finding, goldfinding, all-findingтАЭ and the bahuvr─лhi suv─л╠Бra- тАШpossessing good heroesтАЩ. If Soma finds or possesses these things, he can distribute them to us. The connection between vss. 38 and 39 is nicely signalled by the near identity of 38c and 39a: 38c тАж pavasva v├бsumad dh├нraс╣Зyavat 39a тАж pavasva vasuv├нd dhiraс╣Зyav├нt where the suffix of possession (-mant-, -vant-) subtly gives way to the phonologically similar root-noun -v├нd-, suggesting that Soma possesses those things, which he can now find for us. The epithet nс╣Ы-c├бkс╣гas- тАШhaving his gaze on menтАЩ, found several times previously in this hymn (vss. 23, 36), seems finally to take on its full lexical value in 38, where it is predicated of Soma (nс╣Ыc├бkс╣г─Б asi) and strengthened by vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е тАШon every sideтАЩ, to express SomaтАЩs interest in us and our welfare. The reciprocal relationship between us and Soma is also expressed by the parallel p─Бdas 38d and 39b, both containing bh├║vaneс╣гu as the location of both us (38d) and Soma (39b).

Griffith

As Sovran Lord thereof thou Passest through these worlds, O Indu, harnessing thy tawny well-winged Mares.
May they pour forth for thee milk and oil rich in sweets: O Soma, let the folk abide in thy decree.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, are everywhere, the contemplator of men; you, Pavam─Бna, the showerer, hasten to these (waters); do you pour forth upon us (wealth), comprising various treasures and gold; may we be (able) to live in the worlds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, are one whose gaze is on men on every side. Purifying yourself, bull, you run across these (worlds).
Purify yourself in a manner rich in goods and gold for us. May we be (fit) to live in the worlds.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the -mat and -vat forms adverbially.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the first time in this hymn (save for briefly in vs. 18), this tс╣Ыca shows some interest in what Soma might do for us, particularly in the 2nd two vss.

Note in 38 first the enclitic naс╕е and then the 1st pl. opt. sy─Бma. The poet both asks for benefits directly and by implication, in the cmpds with 2nd member -v├нd- тАШfindingтАЩ: g├│vid-, vasuv├нd-, h├нraс╣Зyav├нd-, vi┼Ыvav├нd- тАЬcow-finding, goods-finding, goldfinding, all-findingтАЭ and the bahuvr─лhi suv─л╠Бra- тАШpossessing good heroesтАЩ. If Soma finds or possesses these things, he can distribute them to us. The connection between vss. 38 and 39 is nicely signalled by the near identity of 38c and 39a: 38c тАж pavasva v├бsumad dh├нraс╣Зyavat 39a тАж pavasva vasuv├нd dhiraс╣Зyav├нt where the suffix of possession (-mant-, -vant-) subtly gives way to the phonologically similar root-noun -v├нd-, suggesting that Soma possesses those things, which he can now find for us. The epithet nс╣Ы-c├бkс╣гas- тАШhaving his gaze on menтАЩ, found several times previously in this hymn (vss. 23, 36), seems finally to take on its full lexical value in 38, where it is predicated of Soma (nс╣Ыc├бkс╣г─Б asi) and strengthened by vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е тАШon every sideтАЩ, to express SomaтАЩs interest in us and our welfare. The reciprocal relationship between us and Soma is also expressed by the parallel p─Бdas 38d and 39b, both containing bh├║vaneс╣гu as the location of both us (38d) and Soma (39b).

Griffith

O Soma, thou beholdest men from every side: O Pavamana, Steer, thou wanderest through these.
Pour out upon us wealth in treasure and in gold: may we have strength to live among the things that be.

Geldner

Du richtest nach allen Seiten dein Herrenauge, Soma, Pavamana, du Bulle durcheilst diese Welten. L├дutere du uns Besitz von Gut und Gold zu! Wir wollen unter den Gesch├╢pfen zu leben ausersehen sein.

Grassmann

Du bist, o Soma, m├дnnerschauend ├╝berall, du Stier durchstr├╢mst hellleuchtend diese ganze Welt; So riesle du uns reiches Gut und Gold herbei, und langes Leben werd’ uns in der Welt zu Theil.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFlow, Indu, who are the winner of cattle, wealth, and gold, the fructifier, plural ced upon the waters; you, Soma, are a hero, omniscient; you these sages approach with praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, as finder of cattle, of goods, of gold. Depositing seed, o drop, you are fitted into the worlds.
You, Soma, are rich in good heroes, finder of all [/all-knowing]. These inspired poets here reverently approach you with a hymn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On vi┼Ыvav├нd- see comm. ad vs. 29. Geldner takes it as тАШall-knowingтАЩ here, but the other -v├нd- cmpds in the vs. favor тАШall-findingтАЩ. Renou, like me, тАШall-findingтАЩ here, though тАШall-knowingтАЩ in 29.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the first time in this hymn (save for briefly in vs. 18), this tс╣Ыca shows some interest in what Soma might do for us, particularly in the 2nd two vss.

Note in 38 first the enclitic naс╕е and then the 1st pl. opt. sy─Бma. The poet both asks for benefits directly and by implication, in the cmpds with 2nd member -v├нd- тАШfindingтАЩ: g├│vid-, vasuv├нd-, h├нraс╣Зyav├нd-, vi┼Ыvav├нd- тАЬcow-finding, goods-finding, goldfinding, all-findingтАЭ and the bahuvr─лhi suv─л╠Бra- тАШpossessing good heroesтАЩ. If Soma finds or possesses these things, he can distribute them to us. The connection between vss. 38 and 39 is nicely signalled by the near identity of 38c and 39a: 38c тАж pavasva v├бsumad dh├нraс╣Зyavat 39a тАж pavasva vasuv├нd dhiraс╣Зyav├нt where the suffix of possession (-mant-, -vant-) subtly gives way to the phonologically similar root-noun -v├нd-, suggesting that Soma possesses those things, which he can now find for us. The epithet nс╣Ы-c├бkс╣гas- тАШhaving his gaze on menтАЩ, found several times previously in this hymn (vss. 23, 36), seems finally to take on its full lexical value in 38, where it is predicated of Soma (nс╣Ыc├бkс╣г─Б asi) and strengthened by vi┼Ыv├бtaс╕е тАШon every sideтАЩ, to express SomaтАЩs interest in us and our welfare. The reciprocal relationship between us and Soma is also expressed by the parallel p─Бdas 38d and 39b, both containing bh├║vaneс╣гu as the location of both us (38d) and Soma (39b).

Griffith

Winner of gold and goods and cattle flow thou on, set as impregner, Indu, mid the worlds of life.
Rich in brave men art thou, Soma, who winnest all: these holy singers wait upon thee with the song.

рдордзреНрд╡рдГ рдордзреБрд░рд╕реНрдп рдКрд░реНрдорд┐рдГ рд░рд╕рдГ рд╡рдирдирд╛рдГ рд╡рдирдиреАрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ рдЙрддреН рдЕрддрд┐рд╖реНрдард┐рдкрддреН рдЙрддреНрдерд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ ред рд╕реЛрдорд╛рднрд┐рд╖рд╡рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддреЗрдГ ред рдЕрдкрдГ рд╡рд╕рд╛рдирдГ рдЖрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрдпрдиреН рдорд╣рд┐рд╖рдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐ рдЧрд╛рд╣рддреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╢рддрд┐ рдХрд▓рд╢рдореН ред рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╕реЛрдордГ рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рд░рдердГред рджрд╢рд╛рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рдореЗрд╡ рд░рдереЛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕ рддрдереЛрдХреНрддрдГ ред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдГ рд╕реЛрдордГ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдВ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордореН рдЖрд░реБрд╣рддреН рдЖрд░реЛрд╣рддрд┐ ред рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рднреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рдмрд╣реБрднреНрд░рдВрд╢реЛрд╜рдкрд░рд┐рдорд┐рддрдЧрдордирдГ рдмреГрд╣рддреН рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдГ рдорд╣рджрдиреНрдирдВ рдЬрдпрддрд┐ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрд░реНрдердореН рее рее резреп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe wave of the swee-flavoured (Soma) exfites voices (of praise); clothed in water the mighty one plural nges (into the pitcher); the king whose chariot is the filter mounts for the conflict, and, armed with a thousand weapons, wins ample sustenance (for us).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The wave of honey has raised (our?) desires; clothing himself in waters, the buffalo plunges through them.
The king whose chariot is the filter has mounted the prize. He of a thousand spikes wins lofty fame.

Jamison Brereton Notes

van├бn─Б- is a hapax, though there seems to be general agreement that it means something like тАШdesireтАЩ, derived from the seс╣н root тИЪvani тАШlove, hold dearтАЩ.

There is an Oldenberg Avestan hapax of the same shape (Y. 44.15) that seems unconnected, in that, contextually, the standard tr. тАШvictoryтАЩ seems correct, and it should therefore be derived from aniс╣н тИЪvan тАШwinтАЩ. But Kellens-Pirart in their OA lexicon (1990) equate it directly with our van├бn─Б- and gloss it тАШcharmeтАЩ - which makes no contextual sense and can, I think, easily be dismissed. In any case it is easy to see how our form came to be built. It is the object of the verb ├║d тАж atiс╣гс╣нhipat тАШmade to stand up / raised upтАЩ. The next vs., 41a, has a very similar VP, bhand├бn─Б ├║d iyarti, where the verb is semantically equivalent to our verb and has the same preverb, and the nominal object is a fem. acc. pl. -├бn─Б- form, which provided the template for van├бn─Б-. Given this parallelism and given the fact that the phrase in vs. 41 has to do with granting blessings to us, I think it likely that the desires Soma raised in 40a are our own (so also Geldner, Renou), which he will fulfill in the next vs. v├н g─Бhate as in 8a; cf. also ├бti g─Бhate in 26a.

Soma is presumably тАЬthousand-spikedтАЭ (sah├бsrabhс╣Ыс╣гс╣нi-) because of the knobs, thorns, or similar extrusions on the plant.

Griffith

The wave of flowing meath hath wakened up desires: the Steer enrobed in milk plunges into the streams.
Borne on his chariot-sieve the King hath risen to war, and with a thousand rays hath won him high renown.

Geldner

Die Welle der S├╝├Яigkeit hat unser Begehren erregt, in Wasser sich kleidend taucht der B├╝ffel hinein. Als ein K├╢nig, dessen Wagen die Seihe ist, hat er den Siegerpreis erklommen, als der Tausendzackige gewinnt er hohen Ruhm.

Grassmann

Des Methes Welle hat erhoben ihr Begehr, in Flut gekleidet taucht der B├╝ffel sich hinein; Der K├╢nig fahrend auf der Seihe drang zum Preis, gewinnt, bewehrt mit tausend Dolchen, hohen Ruhm.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe all-pervading (Soma) exfites both day and night all praises easily borne, productive of prosperity; Indu, when drunk, solicit Indra (to give) us food productive of progeny and riches filling our homes.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He rouses all blessings, consisting of offspring and easy to bear, through our whole lifetime, day upon day. Then, o drop, when drunk, on our behalf beg Indra for a sacred
formulation bringing offspring and for wealth consisting of horses in the homestead.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the relation between the first hemistich and vs. 40 see immed. above.

The published translation тАЬтАж all blessings, consisting of offspring and easy to bearтАЭ is awkward and hard to parse. It might be better as тАЬтАж all blessings, consisting of offspring - a light burden -,тАЭ with subh├бra- used in almost jocular fashion. It can simultaneously also refer to тАЬeasy birth,тАЭ with ref. to praj─Б╠Бvat─лс╕е.

The unusually formed (pseudo-)─Бmreс╕Нita ├бhar-divi тАШevery day, day upon dayтАЩ is esp. interesting in light of the discussion of the two тАШdayтАЩ words ad vs. 19 above. It must be a substitute for the more orthodox ─Бmreс╕Нita ├бhar-ahar (6x) for metrical reasons: the standard cmpd. is metrically awk. With three light syllables in a row, it certainly wonтАЩt fit in any cadence and would be difficult anywhere in the vs. line but where itтАЩs always found, p─Бda-initial (which isnтАЩt all that great either - openings with light syllables in both 2 and 3, not to mention 1 and possibly 4, are quite irregular; see Arnold pp 194-95). It is puzzling, however, that the well-attested (47x) (also somewhat aberrantly formed) ─Бmreс╕Нita to the second тАШdayтАЩ stem here, namely div├йdive, was not used in our vs., since it would fit the cadence perfectly and is quite common in Jagat─л cadences. In any case, at least ├бhar-divi suggests that thereтАЩs no clearcut difference of meaning or reference between ├бhar- and the forms of div-/dyuthat mean тАШdayтАЩ.

In the 2nd hemistich, Soma is not asked directly for benefits, but rather urged to intercede with Indra - to beg him for our sake - for offspring and wealth. This displacement is made all the stranger by the use of a тАЬfuture imperative,тАЭ y─Бcat─Бt, which properly should follow another impv. Perhaps the displacement in time that such an impv. represents - that is, there should be an intervening impv. before it - indirectly reflects the displacement in person - that is, Soma is the middleman, intervening between us and Indra. I suppose it is bad form to ask Indra directly in a hymn devoted to Soma.

There is further displacement here. The тАЬsacred formulation bringing offspringтАЭ (br├бhma praj─Б╠Бvat) that we want Soma to get Indra to give us is not a direct request for Indra to bestow offspring on us, but rather for him to inspire in us a formulation that we can then offer to him, which will, only then, result in offspring.

ItтАЩs a long and winding road to what we want! The interpr. of the hapax bahuvr. ├б┼Ыva-pastya- is disputed. My tr. тАЬconsisting of horses in the homesteadтАЭ essentially follows GrassmannтАЩs тАШRosse im Stalle habendтАЩ, though it would be more lit. as тАШhaving a homestead that has horses in itтАЩ - a v├бjrab─Бhu- type cmpd. GeldnerтАЩs tr. тАЬan vielen RossenтАЭ seems to evade the issue, but his statement in n. 41c тАЬwie sp├дter -┼Ы─Бlin-тАЭ is more forthcoming: -┼Ы─Бlin- means lit.

тАШhaving a house/roomтАЩ, but develops to тАШabounding inтАЩ. Nonetheless, I find it hard to believe that a RVic poet would go to the trouble of using a fairly rare word as 2nd member, only in order to bleach it of its particular meaning. RenouтАЩs тАЬla richesse qui r├йside dans les chevauxтАЭ (and OberтАЩs тАЬdessen fester Wohnsitz Pferde sindтАЭ [I.537 n.

111]) employs an abstract sense of pasty├а- to characterize where wealthтАЩs dwelling is: it resides in - that is, is founded on / consists of тАФ horses. Whereas my interpr.

assumes a concrete homestead, which belongs to the speaker and/or his associates, that is stuffed, as it were, with horses. The difference between the abstract and the concrete interpr. is small but significant, and I continue to prefer the concrete one.

The focus on our welfare found in the last tс╣Ыca is found here in vs. 41 but is otherwise muted.

Griffith

Dear to all life, he sends triumphant praises forth, abundant, bringing offspring, each succeeding day.
From Indra crave for us, Indu, when thou art quaffed, the blessing that gives children, wealth that harbours steeds.

Er bringt zeitlebens Tag f├╝r Tag alle l├╢blichen Dinge, die Nachwuchs haben, auf, deren Last leicht ist: Getrunken sollst du, Saft, f├╝r uns den Indra um Segen, der Nachwuchs bringt, um Reichtum an vielen Rossen bitten.

Grassmann

Er l├дsst erstehen kinderreiche Segnungen, die alle stark sind, allbelebend Tag f├╝r Tag, Geschl├╝rft, o Indu, geh den Indra f├╝r uns an um kinderreich Gebet und rossereichen Stall.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAt the beginning of the day the green-tinted delightful exhilarating (Soma) is recognized by the intelligence (of the praisers) and by their praises; approaching the two men he passes in the midst (of heaven and earth, bestowing) upon the upholder (of the rite) both human and divine (riches).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The two men: i.e., the praiser and the worshipper; or, secular and sacred people (laukikavaidikau)

Jamison Brereton

At the vanguard of the days [=dawn] the tawny, delightful, exhilarating drink makes himself conspicuous with his appearance through the days. Setting in place the two peoples [=gods and men], he speeds between them in upholding the тАЬpraise of menтАЭ and the heavenly (praise).

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs., too, contains the two тАШdayтАЩ words, gen. pl. ├бhn─Бm, dependent on ├бgre, and the adverbial instr. expression ├бnu dy├║bhiс╕е. See comm. ad vss. 19, 41.

I take pr├б тАж cetayate as a reflexive trans./caus. тАШmakes oneself perceivedтАЩ, contrary to the intrans. interpr. in my -├бya- book (p. 163).

As is generally recognized, n├бr─Б ca ┼Ы├бс╣Гsam shows a species of tmesis, from the cmpd n├бr─Б┼Ы├бс╣Гsa-.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The focus on our welfare found in the last tс╣Ыca is found here in vs. 41 but is otherwise muted.

Griffith

When days begin, the strong juice, lovely, golden-hued, is recognized by wisdom more and more each day,
He, stirring both the Races, goes between the two, the bearer of the word of men and word of Gods.

Geldner

Im Anbruch der Tage tut sich der goldige, begehrenswerte Rauschtrank tagt├дglich durch seinen Geist kund. Die beiden V├╢lker einend geht er zwischen Himmel und Erde, er der Tr├дger der M├дnnerrede und der g├╢ttlichen Rede.

рд╕реЛрдордореГрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ рдЕрдЮреНрдЬрддреЗ рдЧреЛрднрд┐рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╡реНрдпрдЮреНрдЬрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдордЮреНрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕рдордЮреНрдЬрддреЗ рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧрдЮреНрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд░реНрдерддреНрд╡рд╛рджрдкреБрдирд░реБрдХреНрддрд┐рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдХреНрд░рддреБрдВ рдмрд▓рдХрд░реНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд░рд┐рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рд▓рд┐рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЖрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдкреБрдирдГ рдордзреБрдирд╛ рдЧрд╡реНрдпреЗрди рдЕрднреНрдпрдЮреНрдЬрддреЗ ред рддрдореЗрд╡ рд╕реЛрдордВ рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреЛрдГ рдЙрджрдХрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╕рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдзрд╛рд░рднреВрддреЗ рдЙрдЪреНрдЫреНрд╡рд╛рд╕реЗ рдЙрдЪреНрдЫреНрд░рд┐рддреЗ рджреЗрд╢реЗ рдкрддрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдореН рее тАШрдкрддреНрд▓реГ рдЧрддреМ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рдгрд┐рдЪрд┐ рд╡реГрджреНрдзреНрдпрднрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдГ рее рдЙрдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╕реЗрдХреНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрдкрд╛рд╡рд╛рдГ рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпреЗрди рдкреБрдирдиреНрддрдГ рдкрд╢реБрдВ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░рдореН ред тАШрдкрд╢реБрдГ рдкрд╢реНрдпрддреЗрдГ ’ (рдирд┐рд░реБ. рей.резрем) рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЖрд╕реБ рд╡рд╕рддреАрд╡рд░реАрд╖реБ рдЧреГрднреНрдгрддреЗ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгрдиреНрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The priests) smear and grease and anoint (the Soma with milk); (the gods) taste the invigorating (juice); they smear it over with sweet (milk). Purifying it with gold, they plural nge it into those (waters) the sprinkler, the beholder, falling into the seething torrent.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Smear and grease and anoint: a├▒jate, vya├▒jate and sama├▒jate are synonyms; into the seething torrent: sindhor ucchv─Бse = liс╣н, in the hreathing of the river; i.e., going to an elevated plural ce, the receptacle of the juice, rasasy─Бdh─Бrabh┼лte ucchrite de┼Ыe gacchantam

Jamison Brereton

They anoint himтАФanoint him separately and jointly. They lick (him who is) resolve; they anoint him with honeyтАФ
him, the ox flying in the burbling up of the river. (The waters,) who
purify the gold (of soma), grasp the stock-animal within themselves.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich is striking with its series of identical verbs in p─Бda a, with p─Бda b ending with the same verb: a├▒j├бte vy ├а├▒jate s├бm a├▒jate, тАж abhy ├а├▒jate.

The first p─Бda lacks a syllable (rest at 4); as Oldenberg suggests, the metrical irregularity is most likely meant to call attention to the word play.

Geldner, Renou, L├╝ders (239) take the various verbs as reflex., with Geldner (n. 43ab) taking the subj. as the soma-drinking singers and Renou as the waters. But though mid. тИЪa├▒j is probably more often reflex./pass. than trans., it can be the latter, and that makes more sense here. Cf., e.g., IX.97.57 s├бm a├▒jate r┼лp├бm тАЬthey jointly anoint his form,тАЭ and recall the many times in this maс╣Зс╕Нala in which soma тАЬis anointed,тАЭ using the true passive ajy├бte (-se) (often as a pun with тАШis drivenтАЩ to тИЪaj). See especially in the next tс╣Ыca of this hymn 47c g├│bhiс╕е тАж samajy├бse, in the same metrical position as s├бm a├▒jate here. I supply the default Soma as obj. throughout the first hemistich; he is found as explicit (though metaphorical) obj. in the 2nd hemistich. As for the subj. of all these verbs, I agree with Renou that it is the waters.

The тАЬox flying in the burbling up of the riverтАЭ of p─Бda c is an ex. of the layers of metaphor just alluded to above: it compresses three different representations of Soma into a single image.

I take the subj. of gс╣Ыbhс╣Зate and referent of hiraс╣Зya-p─Бv─Б╠Бс╕е in d still to be the waters, with ─Бsu functioning as reflexive. Renou explicitly changes his subj. here to тАЬles hommes.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSing (you priests) to the intelligent Pavam─Бna; like a mighty shower he sends forth food; like a snake he glides out of his old skin, sporting like a horse he hastens forth, the showerer, green-tinted.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Sing to the self-purifying one who is attentive to poetic inspiration. Like a great stream he rushes beyond his stalk;
like a snake he slinks beyond his withered skin. Playful like a steed, the tawny bull has run.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner, Renou, Ober (II.54) take ├бndhaс╕е as nom., parallel to dh─Б╠Бr─Б in the simile.

But insofar as it is possible to narrow the referent of this word, it is used of the stalk of the soma (see comm. ad IV.1.19). I take it here as acc., construed with ├бti. This p─Бda, like the following one, depicts the soma juice leaving behind the solid parts of the plant, and ├бti тАШbeyondтАЩ is used in both p─Бdas to express the material beyond which the soma juice has gone.

The simile in d, ├бtyo n├б kr─лс╕╖an, is also found in 26d.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca seems more artful than most of the other, with metaphor layered upon metaphor (vss. 43, 45), varied by similes (vs. 44).

Griffith

Sing forth to Pavamana skilled in holy song: the juice is flowing onward like a mighty stream.
He.glideth like a serpent from his ancient skin, and like a playful horse the Tawny Steer hath run.

Geldner

Lobsinget dem redekundigen Pavamana! Wie ein gro├Яer Strom rinnt der Saft durch die Seihe. Wie eine Schlange entkriecht er der alten Haut; wie ein Renner spielend ist der bullenhafte Falbe geflossen.

Grassmann

Dem rieselnden, begeisterten singt Lobgesang, dem grossen Strome gleichend rinnt er durch das Kraut, Der Schlange gleichend schl├╝pft er durch die alte Haut, wie Renner h├╝pfend eilt dahin der goldne Hengst.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Soma) going foremost, radiant, sanctified by water, plural ced in the firmament as the measure of days is glorified; green-tinted, shedding water, of goodly aspect, the source of moisture, borne in a chariot of light he flows giving wealth, friendly to the house.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The measure of days: beacause, the rule as to the length of day depends on the increase and decrease of the moon’s digits, Soma being here regarded as the moon

Jamison Brereton

Going in the vanguard, the king who is found in the waters displays his power, the measure(r) of the days, fitted into the worlds.
The ghee-backed fallow bay, a flood lovely to see, having light as his chariot, accustomed to wealth, purifies himself.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In a agre-g├бс╕е echoes ├бgre ├бhn─Бm in 42a; in our vs. ├бhn─Бm appears in the following p─Бda, dependent on something else (vim─Б╠Бnaс╕е), though Renou supplies it with agreg├бс╕е as well.

bh├║vaneс╣гv ├бrpitaс╕е also in 39b.

In d I construe r─Бy├й with oky├ас╕е, although I cannot find any parallel usage. But on its own, oky├ас╕е is hard to fit semantically into the vs.; cf. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬgern bleibendтАЭ and RenouтАЩs тАЬ(ce dieu) domestique,тАЭ which seem like afterthoughts..

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca seems more artful than most of the other, with metaphor layered upon metaphor (vss. 43, 45), varied by similes (vs. 44).

Griffith

Dweller in floods, King, foremost, he displays his might, set among living things as measurer of days.
Distilling oil he flows, fair, billowy, golden-hued, borne on a car of light, sharing one hom-e with wealth.

Geldner

Vorangehend zeigt der im Wasser wohnende K├╢nig seine St├дrke, der Ausmesser der Tage, ├╝ber die Welten gesetzt. Ein Falbe, der Schmalz auf dem R├╝cken tr├дgt; dessen Wagen Licht ist, sch├╢n von Aussehen, l├дutert er sich flutend zu Reichtum, gern bleibend.

Der Fluten K├╢nig, f├╝hrend sie, erweist sich stark, die Tage messend, in die Wesen eingef├╝gt; Das sch├╢ne Ross, das wallende mit Fett bedeckt, den Lichtschein fahrend, str├╢mt als Hausherr reiches Gut.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe supporter of heaven the prepared exhilarating (Soma) is let loose, the triple (beverage) rushes to the waters; the worshippers taste the sounding Soma juice, when the reciters of holy texts approach the embodied (beverage) with praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Triple beverage: tridh─Бtu = three vessle, the droс╣Зakala┼Ыa, ─Бhavan─лya and putabhс╣Ыt; or, just, three metallic ores: gold, silver, lead/coopper

Jamison Brereton

It has been sent surgingтАФthe prop of heaven, the exhilarating drink held aloft. It rushes threefold around the worlds.
The thoughts lick the plant that always excites wonder, when the
versifiers have come to array it with a hymn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a skambh├│ div├бс╕е reminds us of 35d div├│ viс╣гс╣нambh├бс╕е with a diff.

lexical real On tridh─Б╠Бtu- see comm. ad IX.70.8.

P─Бda c aс╣Г┼Ы├║с╣Г rihanti mat├бyaс╕е p├бnipnatam is identical to 31d, save for the first word, which in 31 is ┼Ы├н┼Ыum.

In d y├бdi would be best read y├бd *─л, both for sense and for meter, since an opening with light syllables in positions 3 and 4 before an early caesura is very rare (see Arnold 194).

Geldner tr. nirс╣З├нjam тАж yay├║с╕е as тАЬStaat machenтАЭ (make a show), based, he says (n.

46d), on ┼Ы├║bhaс╣Г y─Б. I see no reason to attenuate the sense of nirс╣З├нj-. As Scarlatta (284- 85) argues, this stem can be both a concrete noun тАШgarmentтАЩ and an infin. тАШto arrayтАЩ.

The infinitival usages he cites are mostly the dat. nirс╣З├нje (which, in all quoted cases, I take as a noun) and he is uncertain about the usage of this acc. ex. But since the analysis just proposed of y├бd *─л provides us with an acc. obj., infinitival usage seems best here.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe rapid streams of you when you are purified,being collected together pass through the interstices of the fleece; when you are mixed with water in the ladles, you, Soma, on being effused alight on the pitchers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your streams go forth beyond the fine (hairs) of the ewe; as you are being purified, there go continuous charges.
When, o drop, you are anointed with cows in the two cups, being
pressed you sit in the tubs, Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b is awk. in English. The sense is that the streams of the soma being purified go charging forward continuously, with r├бс╣Гhayaс╕е тАШcharges, speedy forward movementsтАЩ subj. of yanti.
